Chapter XXII Spring and Anne Return to Green Gables The firelight shadow be dance over the kitchen wall at Green Gables , for the spring evening be chilly ; through the open east window drift in the subtly sweet voice of the night .

She 's in Kingsport this winter study music .
I have n't see her , but they say she 's very pretty and that Gilbert be quite crazy over her .
How angry I be when you refuse Gilbert , Anne .
But Roy Gardner be foreordain for you .
I can see that now .
You be right , after all . ''
Anne do not blush , a she usually do when the girl assume that her eventual marriage to Roy Gardner be a settled thing .
All at once she felt rather dull .
Phil 's chatter seem trivial and the reception a bore .
She box poor Rusty 's ear .
`` Get off that cushion instantly , you cat , you !
Why do n't you stay down where you belong ? ''
Anne pick up her orchid and go downstairs , where Aunt Jamesina be preside over a row of coat hang before the fire to warm .

The Sarah-cat do not approve of him .
She always turn her back on him .
But everybody else at Patty 's Place like him very much .
Aunt Jamesina , carry away by his unfailing and deferential courtesy , and the pleading tone of his delightful voice , declare he be the nice young man she ever know , and that Anne be a very fortunate girl .
Such remark make Anne restive .

She be very handsome , in the stately style destine to become rather massive in middle life .
A tall girl , with large dark-blue eye , ivory outline , and a gloss of darkness on her smooth hair .
`` She look just a I 've always want to look , '' think Anne miserably .
`` Rose-leaf complexion -- starry violet eye -- raven hair -- yes , she have them all .
It 's a wonder her name be n't Cordelia Fitzgerald into the bargain !

Anne felt a little comfort by this conclusion .
Chapter XXVII Mutual Confidences March come in that winter like the meek and mild of lamb , bring day that be crisp and golden and tingling , each follow by a frosty pink twilight which gradually lose itself in an elfland of moonshine .
Over the girl at Patty 's Place be fall the shadow of April examination .
They be study hard ; even Phil have settle down to text and notebook with a doggedness not to be expect of her .
`` I 'm go to take the Johnson Scholarship in Mathematics , '' she announce calmly .
`` I could take the one in Greek easily , but I 'd rather take the mathematical one because I want to prove to Jonas that I 'm really enormously clever . ''
`` Jonas like you good for your big brown eye and your crooked smile than for all the brain you carry under your curl , '' say Anne .
`` When I be a girl it be n't consider lady-like to know anything about Mathematics , '' say Aunt Jamesina .
`` But time have change .
I do n't know that it 's all for the good .
Can you cook , Phil ? ''
`` No , I never cook anything in my life except a gingerbread and it be a failure -- flat in the middle and hilly round the edge .
You know the kind .

`` Maybe , '' say Aunt Jamesina cautiously .
`` I be not decry the high education of woman .
My daughter be an M.A . .
She can cook , too .
But I teach her to cook BEFORE I let a college professor teach her Mathematics . ''
In mid-March come a letter from Miss Patty Spofford , say that she and Miss Maria have decide to remain abroad for another year .
`` So you may have Patty 's Place next winter , too , '' she write .
`` Maria and I be go to run over Egypt .
I want to see the Sphinx once before I die . ''
`` Fancy those two dame ` run over Egypt ' !
I wonder if they 'll look up at the Sphinx and knit , '' laugh Priscilla .
`` I 'm so glad we can keep Patty 's Place for another year , '' say Stella .
`` I be afraid they 'd come back .
And then our jolly little nest here would be break up -- and we poor callow nestling throw out on the cruel world of boardinghouse again . ''
`` I 'm off for a tramp in the park , '' announce Phil , toss her book aside .
`` I think when I be eighty I 'll be glad I go for a walk in the park tonight . ''
`` What do you mean ? ''
ask Anne .
`` Come with me and I 'll tell you , honey . ''
They capture in their ramble all the mystery and magic of a March evening .
Very still and mild it be , wrap in a great , white , brooding silence -- a silence which be yet thread through with many little silvery sound which you could hear if you hearken a much with your soul a your ear .
The girl wander down a long pineland aisle that seem to lead right out into the heart of a deep-red , overflow winter sunset .
`` I 'd go home and write a poem this bless minute if I only know how , '' declare Phil , pause in an open space where a rosy light be stain the green tip of the pine .
`` It 's all so wonderful here -- this great , white stillness , and those dark tree that always seem to be think . '' ''
` The wood be God 's first temple , ' '' quote Anne softly .
`` One ca n't help feel reverent and adore in such a place .
I always feel so near Him when I walk among the pine . ''
`` Anne , I 'm the happy girl in the world , '' confess Phil suddenly .
`` So Mr. Blake have ask you to marry him at last ? ''
say Anne calmly .
`` Yes .

Was n't that horrid ?

It 's very delightful to feel so sure , and know it 's your own sureness and not somebody else 's . ''
`` Do you suppose you 'll be able to keep it up ? ''

He say , when I 'm perplexed , just to do what I would wish I have do when I shall be eighty .

He think everything I do right .

Oh , her tongue will be as Byrney a her nose .

`` You 'll have to give up a good many thing you 've always have , when you marry Mr. Blake , Phil . ''

I wo n't miss the other thing .
We 're to be marry a year from next June .
Jo graduate from St. Columbia this spring , you know .
Then he 's go to take a little mission church down on Patterson Street in the slum .
Fancy me in the slum !
But I 'd go there or to Greenland 's icy mountain with him . ''
`` And this be the girl who would NEVER marry a man who be n't rich , '' comment Anne to a young pine tree .
`` Oh , do n't cast up the folly of my youth to me .
I shall be poor as gaily a I 've be rich .
You 'll see .
I 'm go to learn how to cook and make over dress .

But I wo n't .

I 'll be Jo 's little candlestick . ''
`` Phil , you 're incorrigible .
Well , I love you so much that I ca n't make nice , light , congratulatory little speech .
But I 'm heart-glad of your happiness . ''
`` I know .
Those big gray eye of yours be brim over with real friendship , Anne .
Some day I 'll look the same way at you .
You 're go to marry Roy , be n't you , Anne ? ''
`` My dear Philippa , do you ever hear of the famous Betty Baxter , who ` refuse a man before he 'd ax her ' ?
I be not go to emulate that celebrated lady by either refusing or accept any one before he ` ax ' me . ''
`` All Redmond know that Roy be crazy about you , '' say Phil candidly .
`` And you DO love him , do n't you , Anne ? ''
`` I -- I suppose so , '' say Anne reluctantly .
She felt that she ought to be blush while make such a confession ; but she be not ; on the other hand , she always blush hotly when any one say anything about Gilbert Blythe or Christine Stuart in her hearing .
Gilbert Blythe and Christine Stuart be nothing to her -- absolutely nothing .
But Anne have give up try to analyze the reason of her blush .
As for Roy , of course she be in love with him -- madly so .
How could she help it ?
Was he not her ideal ?
Who could resist those glorious dark eye , and that plead voice ?
Were not half the Redmond girl wildly envious ?
And what a charming sonnet he have send her , with a box of violet , on her birthday !
Anne know every word of it by heart .
It be very good stuff of it kind , too .
Not exactly up to the level of Keats or Shakespeare -- even Anne be not so deeply in love a to think that .
But it be very tolerable magazine verse .
And it be address to HER -- not to Laura or Beatrice or the Maid of Athens , but to her , Anne Shirley .
To be tell in rhythmical cadence that her eye be star of the morning -- that her cheek have the flush it steal from the sunrise -- that her lip be red than the rose of Paradise , be thrillingly romantic .
Gilbert would never have dream of write a sonnet to her eyebrow .
But then , Gilbert could see a joke .
She have once tell Roy a funny story -- and he have not see the point of it .
She recall the chummy laugh she and Gilbert have have together over it , and wonder uneasily if life with a man who have no sense of humor might not be somewhat uninteresting in the long run .
But who could expect a melancholy , inscrutable hero to see the humorous side of thing ?
It would be flatly unreasonable .
Chapter XXVIII A June Evening `` I wonder what it would be like to live in a world where it be always June , '' say Anne , a she come through the spice and bloom of the twilit orchard to the front door step , where Marilla and Mrs. Rachel be sit , talk over Mrs. Samson Coates ' funeral , which they have attend that day .

`` I daresay ; but just now I feel that it would take me a long time to get tire of it , if it be all as charm a today .
Everything love June .

`` I 'm just sick and tired of living , '' say the youthful pessimist .
`` At ten year ?
Dear me , how sad ! ''

`` I 'm dis -- dis -- discourage '' -- bring out the big word with a valiant effort .

ask Anne , sit down beside him . ''
'Cause the new teacher that come when Mr. Holmes get sick give me ten sum to do for Monday .

She be afraid Providence would n't interfere ; and she do n't dare to .
Anne have wander down to the Dryad 's Bubble and be curl up among the fern at the root of the big white birch where she and Gilbert have so often sat in summer go by .

To be sure , Roy write twice a week ; his letter be exquisite composition which would have read beautifully in a memoir or biography .
Anne felt herself more deeply in love with him than ever when she read them ; but her heart never give the queer , quick , painful bound at sight of his letter which it have give one day when Mrs. Hiram Sloane have hand her out an envelope address in Gilbert 's black , upright handwriting .

Anne fling the harmless screed across her room and sit down to write an especially nice epistle to Roy .
Diana be to be marry in five more day .
The gray house at Orchard Slope be in a turmoil of baking and brewing and boiling and stewing , for there be to be a big , old-timey wedding .
Anne , of course , be to be bridesmaid , a have be arrange when they be twelve year old , and Gilbert be come from Kingsport to be best man .
Anne be enjoy the excitement of the various preparation , but under it all she carry a little heartache .

Anne look up at Diana 's light and think how it have beacon to her for many year ; but soon it would shine through the summer twilights no more .

`` Oh , '' she think , `` how horrible it be that people have to grow up -- and marry -- and CHANGE ! ''
Chapter XXIX Diana 's Wedding `` After all , the only real rose be the pink one , '' say Anne , a she tie white ribbon around Diana 's bouquet in the westward-looking gable at Orchard Slope .

Following the simple , old-fashioned way in vogue then , Anne go down to the parlor on Gilbert 's arm .

`` Are you go to be in Avonlea all summer ? ''

`` No .

So I 'm go to substitute for her .
In one way I do n't mind .

Anne laugh and sigh .

Oh , Avonlea be go to be so lonely now -- with Diana go !
Chapter XXX Mrs. Skinner 's Romance Anne step off the train at Valley Road station and look about to see if any one have come to meet her .
She be to board with a certain Miss Janet Sweet , but she saw no one who answer in the least to her preconception of that lady , a form from Esther 's letter .
The only person in sight be an elderly woman , sit in a wagon with mail bag pile around her .
Two hundred would have be a charitable guess at her weight ; her face be a round and red a a harvest-moon and almost a featureless .
She wear a tight , black , cashmere dress , make in the fashion of ten year ago , a little dusty black straw hat trim with bow of yellow ribbon , and fade black lace mit .
`` Here , you , '' she call , wave her whip at Anne .
`` Are you the new Valley Road schoolma'am ? ''
`` Yes . ''
`` Well , I think so .
Valley Road be note for it good-looking schoolma'am , just a Millersville be note for it humly one .
Janet Sweet ask me this morning if I could bring you out .

Thomas want to hoe his turnip today so he ask me to come .
So I jest sot down and take a standing-up snack and start .
I sorter like it .
O ' course it 's rather teju .
Part of the time I sits and think and the rest I jest sits .
Jog along , black mare .
I want to git home airly .

You see , we have n't be marry very long . ''
`` Oh ! ''
say Anne politely .
`` Just a month .
Thomas court me for quite a spell , though .
It be real romantic . ''
Anne try to picture Mrs. Skinner on speaking term with romance and fail .
`` Oh ? ''
she say again .
`` Yes .
Y ` see , there be another man after me .
Jog along , black mare .
I 'd be a widder so long folk have give up expect me to marry again .

Jog along , black mare . ''
`` Why do n't you marry him ? ''
ask Anne .
`` Well , y ` see , he do n't love me , '' answer Mrs. Skinner , solemnly .
Anne open her eye widely and look at Mrs. Skinner .
But there be not a glint of humor on that lady 's face .
Evidently Mrs. Skinner saw nothing amusing in her own case .
`` He 'd be a widder-man for three yers , and his sister keep house for him .

It be worth look after , too , mind you that .
It 's a handsome house .
Jog along , black mare .

But , y ` see , I love Thomas , and I do n't care one red cent for W.O . .
So I argue it out with myself .
` Sarah Crowe , ' say I -- my first be a Crowe -- ` you can marry your rich man if you like but you wo n't be happy .
Folks ca n't get along together in this world without a little bit of love .
You 'd just well tie up to Thomas , for he love you and you love him and nothing else ai n't go to do you . '
Jog along , black mare .
So I tell Thomas I 'd take him .
All the time I be get ready I never dare drive past W.O . 's place for fear the sight of that fine house of his would put me in the swither again .
But now I never think of it at all , and I 'm just that comfortable and happy with Thomas .
Jog along , black mare . ''
`` How do William Obadiah take it ? ''
query Anne .
`` Oh , he rumpus a bit .
But he 's go to see a skinny old maid in Millersville now , and I guess she 'll take him fast enough .
She 'll make him a good wife than his first do .

He just ask her to marry him 'cause his father want him to , never dream but that she 'd say ` no . '
But mind you , she say ` yes . '
There be a predicament for you .
Jog along , black mare .
She be a great housekeeper , but most awful mean .
She wear the same bonnet for eighteen year .
Then she get a new one and W.O . meet her on the road and do n't know her .
Jog along , black mare .
I feel that I 'd a narrer escape .
I might have marry him and be most awful miserable , like my poor cousin , Jane Ann .
Jane Ann marry a rich man she do n't care anything about , and she have n't the life of a dog .
She come to see me last week and say , say she , ` Sarah Skinner , I envy you .
I 'd rather live in a little hut on the side of the road with a man I be fond of than in my big house with the one I 've get . '
Jane Ann 's man ai n't such a bad sort , nuther , though he 's so contrary that he wear his fur coat when the thermometer 's at ninety .
The only way to git him to do anything be to coax him to do the opposite .
But there ai n't any love to smooth thing down and it 's a poor way of living .
Jog along , black mare .
There 's Janet 's place in the hollow -- ` Wayside , ' she call it .
Quite pictureaskew , ai n't it ?
I guess you 'll be glad to git out of this , with all them mail bag jam round you . ''

say Mrs. Skinner , highly flatter .

Chapter XXXI Anne to Philippa `` Anne Shirley to Philippa Gordon , greeting .
`` Well-beloved , it 's high time I be write you .
Here be I , instal once more a a country ` schoolma'am ' at Valley Road , board at ` Wayside , ' the home of Miss Janet Sweet .
Janet be a dear soul and very nicelooking ; tall , but not over-tall ; stoutish , yet with a certain restraint of outline suggestive of a thrifty soul who be not go to be overlavish even in the matter of avoirdupois .
She have a knot of soft , crimpy , brown hair with a thread of gray in it , a sunny face with rosy cheek , and big , kind eye as blue a forget-me-not .
Moreover , she be one of those delightful , old-fashioned cook who do n't care a bit if they ruin your digestion as long a they can give you feast of fat thing .
`` I like her ; and she like me -- principally , it seem , because she have a sister name Anne who die young . ''
` I 'm real glad to see you , ' she say briskly , when I land in her yard .
` My , you do n't look a mite like I expect .
I be sure you 'd be dark -- my sister Anne be dark .
And here you 're redheaded ! '
`` For a few minute I think I be n't go to like Janet as much a I have expect at first sight .
Then I remind myself that I really must be more sensible than to be prejudice against any one simply because she call my hair red .
Probably the word ` auburn ' be not in Janet 's vocabulary at all . ''
` Wayside ' be a dear sort of little spot .
The house be small and white , set down in a delightful little hollow that drop away from the road .
Between road and house be an orchard and flower-garden all mix up together .
The front door walk be border with quahog clam-shells -- ` cow-hawks , ' Janet call them ; there be Virginia Creeper over the porch and moss on the roof .
My room be a neat little spot ` off the parlor ' -- just big enough for the bed and me .
Over the head of my bed there be a picture of Robby Burns stand at Highland Mary 's grave , shadow by an enormous weeping willow tree .
Robby 's face be so lugubrious that it be no wonder I have bad dream .
Why , the first night I be here I dream I COULD N'T LAUGH .
`` The parlor be tiny and neat .
Its one window be so shade by a huge willow that the room have a grotto-like effect of emerald gloom .
There be wonderful tidy on the chair , and gay mat on the floor , and book and card carefully arrange on a round table , and vas of dried grass on the mantel-piece .
Between the vas be a cheerful decoration of preserved coffin plate -- five in all , pertain respectively to Janet 's father and mother , a brother , her sister Anne , and a hired man who die here once !
If I go suddenly insane some of these day ` know all men by these present ' that those coffin-plates have cause it .
`` But it 's all delightful and I say so .
Janet love me for it , just a she detest poor Esther because Esther have say so much shade be unhygienic and have object to sleep on a feather bed .
Now , I glory in feather-beds , and the more unhygienic and feathery they be the more I glory .
Janet say it be such a comfort to see me eat ; she have be so afraid I would be like Miss Haythorne , who would n't eat anything but fruit and hot water for breakfast and try to make Janet give up fry thing .
Esther be really a dear girl , but she be rather give to fad .
The trouble be that she have n't enough imagination and HAS a tendency to indigestion .
`` Janet tell me I could have the use of the parlor when any young men call !
I do n't think there be many to call .
I have n't see a young man in Valley Road yet , except the next-door hired boy -- Sam Toliver , a very tall , lank , tow-haired youth .
He come over one evening recently and sit for an hour on the garden fence , near the front porch where Janet and I be do fancy-work .
The only remark he volunteer in all that time be , ` Hev a peppermint , miss !
Dew now-fine thing for carARRH , peppermint , ' and , ` Powerful lot o ' jump-grasses round here ternight .
Yep . '
`` But there be a love affair go on here .
It seem to be my fortune to be mix up , more or less actively , with elderly love affair .
Mr. and Mrs. Irving always say that I bring about their marriage .
Mrs. Stephen Clark of Carmody persist in be most grateful to me for a suggestion which somebody else would probably have make if I have n't .
I do really think , though , that Ludovic Speed would never have get any far along than placid courtship if I have not help him and Theodora Dix out .
`` In the present affair I be only a passive spectator .
I 've try once to help thing along and make an awful mess of it .
So I shall not meddle again .
I 'll tell you all about it when we meet . ''
Chapter XXXII Tea with Mrs. Douglas On the first Thursday night of Anne 's sojourn in Valley Road Janet ask her to go to prayer-meeting .
Janet blossom out like a rise to attend that prayer-meeting .
She wear a pale-blue , pansy-sprinkled muslin dress with more ruffle than one would ever have suppose economical Janet could be guilty of , and a white leghorn hat with pink rose and three ostrich feather on it .
Anne felt quite amaze .
Later on , she find out Janet 's motive in so array herself -- a motive as old a Eden .
Valley Road prayer-meetings seem to be essentially feminine .
There be thirty-two woman present , two half-grown boy , and one solitary man , beside the minister .
Anne find herself study this man .
He be not handsome or young or graceful ; he have remarkably long legs -- so long that he have to keep them coil up under his chair to dispose of them -- and he be stoop-shouldered .
His hand be big , his hair want barbering , and his moustache be unkempt .
But Anne think she like his face ; it be kind and honest and tender ; there be something else in it , too -- just what , Anne find it hard to define .
She finally conclude that this man have suffer and be strong , and it have be make manifest in his face .
There be a sort of patient , humorous endurance in his expression which indicate that he would go to the stake if need be , but would keep on look pleasant until he really have to begin squirm .
When prayer-meeting be over this man come up to Janet and say , `` May I see you home , Janet ? ''
Janet take his arm -- `` a primly and shyly a if she be no more than sixteen , have her first escort home , '' Anne tell the girl at Patty 's Place later on .
`` Miss Shirley , permit me to introduce Mr. Douglas , '' she say stiffly .
Mr. Douglas nod and say , `` I be look at you in prayer-meeting , miss , and think what a nice little girl you be . ''
Such a speech from ninety-nine people out of a hundred would have annoy Anne bitterly ; but the way in which Mr. Douglas say it make her feel that she have receive a very real and pleasing compliment .
She smile appreciatively at him and drop obligingly behind on the moonlit road .
So Janet have a beau !
Anne be delight .
Janet would make a paragon of a wife -- cheery , economical , tolerant , and a very queen of cook .
It would be a flagrant waste on Nature 's part to keep her a permanent old maid .
`` John Douglas ask me to take you up to see his mother , '' say Janet the next day .
`` She 's bed-rid a lot of the time and never go out of the house .
But she 's powerful fond of company and always want to see my boarder .
Can you go up this evening ? ''
Anne assent ; but later in the day Mr. Douglas call on his mother 's behalf to invite them up to tea on Saturday evening .
`` Oh , why do n't you put on your pretty pansy dress ? ''
ask Anne , when they leave home .

The old Douglas homestead be half a mile from `` Wayside '' crest a windy hill .
The house itself be large and comfortable , old enough to be dignify , and girdle with maple grove and orchard .
There be big , trim barn behind it , and everything bespoke prosperity .

I 'm delighted to meet you .

Janet turn red than ever but do it .
Anne write a description of that meal to Stella .
`` We have cold tongue and chicken and strawberry preserve , lemon pie and tart and chocolate cake and raisin cooky and pound cake and fruit cake -- and a few other thing , include more pie -- caramel pie , I think it be .
After I have eat twice as much a be good for me , Mrs. Douglas sigh and say she fear she have nothing to tempt my appetite . ''

WO N'T you have another piece of pie , Miss Shirley ?
You have n't eat ANYTHING . '

`` Miss Shirley will keep me company while you be out -- wo n't you ? ''

She settle down in her armchair with a sigh .
`` I be a very frail old woman , Miss Shirley .
For over twenty year I 've be a great sufferer .
For twenty long , weary year I 've be die by inch . ''
`` How painful ! ''

`` Janet be a lovely woman , '' say Anne warmly .
`` Lovely !
A beautiful character , '' assent Mrs. Douglas .
`` And a perfect housekeeper -- something I never be .
My health would not permit it , Miss Shirley .

I hope and believe that he will be happy .
He be my only son , Miss Shirley , and his happiness lie very near my heart . ''
`` Of course , '' say Anne stupidly .
For the first time in her life she be stupid .
Yet she could not imagine why .

`` Come and see me soon again , dear Janet , '' say Mrs. Douglas lovingly , when they leave .

But then I suppose John will be bring you here to stay all the time one of these day . ''

Chapter XXXIII `` He Just Kept Coming and Coming '' Three day later Anne come home from school and find Janet cry .
Tears and Janet seem so incongruous that Anne be honestly alarm .
`` Oh , what be the matter ? ''
she cry anxiously .

How much time do he want ? ''

And I do n't believe he ever will now .
I 've never say a word to a mortal about it , but it seem to me I 've just get to talk it out with some one at last or go crazy .

Mother die when we 'd be go together for eight year .

And that 's the way it have be go on ever since .
People blame ME for it .
They say I wo n't marry him because his mother be so sickly and I do n't want the bother of wait on her .
Why , I 'd LOVE to wait on John 's mother !
But I let them think so .
I 'd rather they 'd blame me than pity me !

Chapter XXXIV John Douglas Speaks at Last Anne be not without a feeble hope that something might come of it after all .

Her walk to and from school be pleasant .
She always go by way of the swamp ; it be a lovely place -- a boggy soil , green with the greenest of mossy hillock ; a silvery brook meander through it and spruce stand erectly , their bough a-trail with gray-green moss , their root overgrown with all sort of woodland loveliness .
Nevertheless , Anne find life in Valley Road a little monotonous .
To be sure , there be one diverting incident .
She have not see the lank , tow-headed Samuel of the peppermint since the evening of his call , save for chance meeting on the road .
But one warm August night he appear , and solemnly seat himself on the rustic bench by the porch .
He wear his usual working habiliment , consist of varipatched trouser , a blue jean shirt , out at the elbow , and a ragged straw hat .
He be chew a straw and he keep on chew it while he look solemnly at Anne .
Anne lay her book aside with a sigh and take up her doily .
Conversation with Sam be really out of the question .
After a long silence Sam suddenly speak .
`` I 'm leave over there , '' he say abruptly , wave his straw in the direction of the neighboring house .
`` Oh , be you ? ''
say Anne politely .
`` Yep . ''
`` And where be you go now ? ''
`` Wall , I 've be think some of gitting a place of my own .
There 's one that 'd suit me over at Millersville .
But ef I rent it I 'll want a woman . ''

`` Yep . ''

`` Yep . ''

And she 's hold me to that promise ever since , though I 've go on my knee to her in my turn to beg her to let me off . ''

The Hurrying of Ludovic Anne Shirley be curl up on the window-seat of Theodora Dix 's sitting-room one Saturday evening , look dreamily afar at some fair starland beyond the hill of sunset .
